[9:0:169,475] 3850   Coachella Valley Mountains Conservancy  

[10:0:66,496] The mission of the Coachella Valley Mountains Conservancy is to acquire and hold as open space the mountainous lands  

[10:1:66,506] surrounding the Coachella Valley and the natural lands within the Coachella Valley. In addition, the Conservancy works to  

[10:2:66,517] protect wildlife and enhance recreational and educational experiences on those lands, to conserve local water resources and to  

[10:3:66,527] promote sustainability and climate change adaptability within the desert and surrounding mountain areas.

[10:0:66,543] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[10:1:66,563] 3220 - SIERRA NEVADA CONSERVANCY PROGRAM  

[11:0:66,583] Established pursuant to Chapter 726, Statutes of 2004, the Conservancy is authorized to:  

[11:1:65,601] • Provide increased opportunities for tourism and recreation.  

[12:0:65,617] • Protect, conserve, and restore the region's physical, cultural, archaeological, historical, and living resources.  

[12:1:65,633] • Aid in the preservation of working landscapes.  

[12:2:65,649] • Reduce the risk of natural disasters, such as wildfires.  

[12:3:65,665] • Protect and improve water and air quality.  

[12:4:65,682] • Assist the regional economy through the operation of the Conservancy's program.  

[12:5:65,698] • Undertake efforts to enhance public use and enjoyment of lands owned by the public.

[5:0:196,218] 3860   Department of Water Resources  

[6:0:66,240] The Department of Water Resources protects, conserves, develops, and manages California's water. The Department  

[7:0:66,250] evaluates existing water resources, forecasts future water needs, and explores potential solutions to meet the state’s growing  

[7:1:66,260] needs for personal use, irrigation, industry, recreation, power generation, and fish and wildlife. The Department also works to  

[8:0:66,270] prevent and minimize flood damage, oversee the safety of dams, and educate the public about the importance of water and its  

[8:1:66,281] efficient use.  

[9:0:66,301] Because the Department's programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Department has a capital outlay program to  

[9:1:66,311] support this need. For the specifics on the Department's capital outlay program see "Infrastructure Overview."

[12:1:65,613] • New River Improvement Project - The Budget includes $18 million one-time General Fund and $10 million Proposition 68 to  

[12:2:76,623] support the New River Improvement Project, which aims to address solid waste and water quality challenges in the City of  

[12:3:76,634] Calexico to support health, recreation and economic benefits in the area.

[13:1:76,660] to support the implementation of Sustainable Groundwater Management Act regulatory oversight and provide technical  

[13:2:76,670] assistance on the Groundwater Sustainability Plans.  

[14:0:65,686] • Proposition 68: Continuation of Various Flood and Restoration Programs – The Budget includes $54.6 million Proposition 68  

[14:1:76,697] to enhance the state’s flood control and prevention system through the Floodplain Management, Yolo Bypass Multi-Benefit,  

[14:2:76,707] and Floodwater Groundwater Recharge.

[5:0:66,181] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,201] 3230 - CONTINUING FORMULATION OF THE CALIFORNIA WATER PLAN  

[7:0:66,218] The California Water Plan is the state's strategic plan for the efficient use, management and development of the state's water  

[7:1:66,229] resources. The Plan is updated every five years and provides a framework for water managers, legislators, and the public to  

[7:2:66,239] consider options and make decisions regarding California's water future. The Plan evaluates current and future water  

[7:3:66,249] conditions, challenges and opportunities. It presents basic data and information on California's water resources including water  

[7:4:66,259] supply evaluations and assessments of existing and future agricultural, urban, and environmental water uses. The Plan  

[7:5:66,269] identifies and evaluates multiple future scenarios and over 30 resource management strategies such as conservation,  

[7:6:66,280] recycling, desalination, transfers, storage, conveyance, water quality, watershed management, ecosystem restoration,  

[7:7:66,290] groundwater, and urban land use management to help meet future demands in light of uncertainties and unexpected  

[7:8:66,300] catastrophic events. This program also identifies ways for the state to: (1) help local agencies and governments prepare  

[7:9:66,310] integrated regional water management plans on a watershed basis and diversify their regional water portfolios to ensure  

[7:10:66,320] sustainable water uses, reliable water supplies, better water quality, environmental stewardship, efficient urban development,  

[7:11:66,331] protection of agriculture, and a strong economy, (2) help cities, counties and local agencies prepare a Water Element for their  

[7:12:66,341] General Plans, Urban Water Management Plans and Agricultural Water Management Plans, and (3) help local agencies and  

[7:13:66,351] tribal governments improve water and land use planning coordination.  

[8:0:66,369] 3240 - IMPLEMENTATION OF THE STATE WATER RESOURCES DEVELOPMENT SYSTEM  

[9:0:66,386] The State Water Project is a water storage and delivery system that consists of 34 storage facilities (reservoirs and lakes), 21  

[9:1:66,397] pumping plants, 4 pumping-generating plants, 5 hydroelectric power plants, and over 700 miles of conveyance (canals,  

[9:2:66,407] pipelines, and tunnels). The Project provides water to over 25 million Californians and 750,000 acres of irrigated farmland.  

[10:0:66,425] The Department plans, designs, constructs, operates, maintains, and manages State Water Project facilities that provide water  

[10:1:66,435] to facilities located from Plumas County to Riverside County.  

[11:0:66,452] The Delta Conveyance Program is charged with improving the Delta ecosystem and ensuring water supply reliability in a safe,  

[11:1:66,463] timely, and cost-effective manner. This includes implementation of the Delta Conveyance, project specific environmental  

[11:2:66,473] commitments, and compliance with the Environmental Impact Report and Environmental Impact Statement and other state and  

[11:3:66,483] federal regulations and permits.  

[12:0:66,501] 3245 - PUBLIC SAFETY AND PREVENTION OF DAMAGE  

[13:0:66,518] This program supports the California Water Action Plan by protecting life and property from damage by floods, ensures proper  

[13:1:66,529] construction and maintenance of jurisdictional dams and levees, and provides loans for levee construction. Activities include  

[13:2:66,539] assessing the state and regional investment needs to reduce risk, preventive floodplain management to discourage unwise use  

[13:3:66,549] of areas subject to flooding, protection of floodplains, issuance of flood warnings, operation of flood control facilities,  

[13:4:66,559] coordination and supervision of flood fight activities, and annual levee and flood channel maintenance and inspection in  

[13:5:66,569] cooperation with other local, state, and federal partner agencies. This program also buys land, easements, and rights-of-way  

[13:6:66,580] for federal flood control projects and supervises the design and construction of new dams and periodic inspection and the  

[13:7:66,590] reevaluation of all existing jurisdictional dams for proper operation and maintenance. Fiscal oversight and coordination activities  

[13:8:66,600] associated with the Disaster Preparedness and Flood Prevention Bond Act of 2006 are administered under this program. The  

[13:9:66,610] program also reviews federal dam projects in coordination with federal and other state agencies with regard to dam safety.  

[14:0:66,628] 3250 - CENTRAL VALLEY FLOOD PROTECTION BOARD  

[15:0:66,648] The Central Valley Flood Protection Board has regulatory authority over the State Plan of Flood Control facilities (SPFC),  

[15:1:66,659] designated floodways, and regulated streams in the Central Valley. The Board regulates encroachments on the system by  

[15:2:66,669] issuing permits and initiating enforcement action when necessary to maintain the integrity of the levees and floodways that  

[15:3:66,679] protect the valley's people and property. The Board manages the state's portfolio of real property held by the Sacramento-San  

[15:4:66,689] Joaquin Drainage District. The Board serves as the non-federal sponsor to the United States Army Corps of Engineers on large  

[15:5:66,699] joint state-federal levee improvement projects and assists the more than one hundred local maintaining agencies that operate  

[16:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,83] and maintain the SPFC. The Board conducts regular public meetings, workshops and tours, providing a public forum for  

[3:1:66,93] stakeholders.  

[3:2:66,111] 3255 - SERVICES  

[4:0:66,128] This program provides technical support within the Department and expertise in the fields of water resources planning,  

[4:1:66,139] development and management; watermaster services; scientific analyses performed by DWR's chemical laboratory;  

[4:2:66,149] information technology; and mapping, surveying and engineering services for other agencies.  

[4:3:66,167] 3260 - CALIFORNIA ENERGY RESOURCES SCHEDULING  

[5:0:66,184] California Energy Resources Scheduling is responsible for managing the Electrical Power Fund and the Department of Water  

[5:1:66,194] Resources (DWR) Charge Fund. For a limited period of time, the Electrical Power Charge Fund purchased electric power on  

[5:2:66,205] behalf of the state's investor-owned utilities. The Department retains the legal and financial responsibility for administering  

[5:3:66,215] revenue bonds issued to repay the General Fund for money borrowed for power purchases during the energy crisis and  

[5:4:66,225] funding of reserve accounts necessary to maintain an investment grade credit rating associated with the revenue bonds.   The  

[5:5:66,235] DWR Charge Fund will manage the collection of bond charges from ratepayers of Investor-Owned Utility companies, and  

[5:6:66,245] proceeds from issuance of bonds.

[5:0:66,169] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW  

[6:0:66,188] The Department of Water Resources has two major infrastructure programs: the State Water Project and the flood control  

[6:1:66,199] system in the Central Valley. The State Water Project is a water storage and delivery system that consists of 34 storage  

[6:2:66,209] facilities, reservoirs, and lakes, 21 pumping plants, 4 pumping-generating plants, 5 hydroelectric power plants, and over 700  

[6:3:66,219] miles of canals, pipelines, and tunnels. The Project provides water to 25 million Californians and 750,000 acres of irrigated  

[6:4:66,229] farmland. The Project also provides recreational opportunities to approximately 6 million visitors annually at 15 separate  

[6:5:66,239] reservoir-based facilities as well as public fishing access to much of the Aqueduct. Existing flood control infrastructure in the  

[6:6:66,250] Central Valley consists of 1,595 miles of levees, 348,000 acres of channels and floodways, over 800,000 linear feet of bank  

[6:7:66,260] protection, over 60 mitigation and environmental restoration sites, and 55 various flood control structures including dams, weirs,  

[6:8:66,270] pumping plants, diversion structures, gate structures, and drop structures. In general, these facilities provide more flood  

[6:9:66,280] protection in urbanized areas and less in agricultural areas.

[9:0:159,435] 3875   Sacramento-San Joaquin Delta Conservancy  

[10:0:66,456] The mission of the Sacramento-San Joaquin Delta Conservancy is to act as the primary state agency to implement ecosystem  

[10:1:66,466] restoration in the Delta and   support efforts that advance both environmental protection and the economic well-being of Delta  

[10:2:66,476] residents in a complementary manner. The Conservancy's activities include protecting and enhancing habitat and habitat  

[10:3:66,487] restoration; protecting and preserving Delta agriculture and working landscapes; providing increased opportunities for tourism  

[10:4:66,497] and recreation; promoting Delta legacy communities and economic vitality in the Delta; increasing the resilience of the Delta to  

[10:5:66,507] the effects of climate change and natural disasters such as floods and earthquakes; protecting and improving water quality;  

[10:6:66,517] assisting the Delta regional economy; identifying priority projects and initiatives for which funding is needed; conducting  

[10:7:66,527] activities to protect, conserve, and restore the region's physical, agricultural, cultural, historical, and living resources; assisting  

[10:8:66,538] local entities in the implementation of their habitat conservation plans and natural community conservation plans; facilitating  

[10:9:66,548] protection and safe harbor agreements under the federal Endangered Species Act of 1973 and the California Endangered  

[10:10:66,558] Species Act for adjacent land owners and local public agencies; and promoting environmental education.

[8:0:211,320] 3885   Delta Stewardship Council  

[8:1:66,342] Established in 2009 by the Delta Reform Act, the mission of the Delta Stewardship Council, through a seven-member board, is  

[8:2:66,352] to further the state's coequal goals of providing a more reliable water supply for California and protecting, restoring, and  

[8:3:66,362] enhancing the Sacramento-San Joaquin Delta ecosystem. The goals are to be achieved in a manner that protects and  

[9:0:66,372] enhances the unique cultural, recreational, natural resource, and agricultural values of the Delta. In 2013, the Council adopted  

[9:1:66,383] a legally enforceable Delta Plan to further the coequal goals and guide state and local agency activities related to the Delta.  

[9:2:66,393] Under state law, agencies are required to coordinate their actions pursuant to the Delta Plan with the Council and the other  

[9:3:66,403] relevant agencies. In 2019, the Council completed its five-year review of the Delta Plan as required   under state law.   The  

[10:0:66,413] Council is informed by scientific input from the Delta Science Program and the Delta Independent Science Board. The mission  

[10:1:66,423] of the Delta Science Program is to provide the best possible unbiased scientific information to inform water and environmental  

[10:2:66,434] decisionmaking in the Delta.
